<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

<p></p>
<p>Because doing if-else chains on a single variable testing for equality is so common, C++ provides an alternative conditional branching operator called a <strong>switch</strong>.  Here is the same program as above in switch form:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">

id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-20"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">break</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-21"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">default</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-22"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Unknown"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-23"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">break</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-24"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73534194a265556208-25"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0030 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The overall idea behind switch statements is simple: the switch expression is evalutated to produce a value, and each case label is tested against this value for equality.  If a case label matches, the statements after the case label are executed.  If no case label matches the switch expression, the code under the default label is executed (if it exists).</p>
<p>Let&#8217;s examine each of these concepts in more detail.</p>
<p>We start a switch statement by using the <strong>switch</strong> keyword, followed by the expression that we would like to evaluate.  Typically this expression is just a single variable, but it can be something more complex like <code>nX + 2</code> or <code>nX - nY</code>.  The one restriction on this expression is that it must evaluate to an integral type (that is, char, short, int, long, or enum).  Floating point variables and other non-integral types may not be used here.</p>
<p>Following the switch expression, we declare a block.  Inside the block, we use <strong>labels</strong> to define all of the values we want to test for equality.  There are two kinds of labels.</p>
<p>The first kind of label is the <strong>case label</strong>, which is declared using the <strong>case</strong> keyword, and followed by a constant expression.  A constant expression is one that evaluates to a constant value -- in other words, either a literal (such as 5), an enum (such as COLOR_RED), or a constant integral variable (such as nX, when nX has been defined as a const int).</p>
<p>The constant expression following the case label is tested for equality against the expression following the switch keyword.  If they match, the code under the case label is executed.  Typically, we end each case with a break statement, which tells the compiler that we are done with the case.</p>
<p>It is worth noting that all case label expressions must evaluate to a unique value.  That is, you can not do this:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It is possible to have multiple case labels refer to the same statements.  The following function uses multiple cases to test if the cChar parameter is an ASCII number.</p>

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0021 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>If any of the case labels match, the next statement is executed.  In this case, that is the statement <code>return true;</code>, which returns the value true to the caller.</p>
<p>The second kind of label is the <strong>default label</strong>, which is declared using the <strong>default</strong> keyword.  The code under this label gets executed if none of the cases match the switch expression.  The default label is optional.  It is also typically declared as the last label in the switch block, though this is not strictly necessary.</p>
<p>One of the trickiest things about case statements is the way in which execution proceeds when a case is matched.  When a case is matched (or the default is executed), execution begins at the first statement following that label and continues until one of the following conditions is true:<br />
1) The end of the switch block is reached<br />
2) A return statement occurs<br />
3) A goto statement occurs<br />
4) A break statement occurs</p>
<p>Note that if none of these conditions are met, cases will overflow into other cases!  Consider the following program:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d735341962970905669" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

</span><span class="crayon-st">case</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d735341962970905669-10"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">4</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// This is also executed</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d735341962970905669-11"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-st">default</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d735341962970905669-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">5</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// This is also executed</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d735341962970905669-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0024 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This program prints the result:</p>
<pre>
2
3
4
5
</pre>
<p>Probably not what we wanted!  When execution flows from one case into another case, this is called <strong>fall-through</strong>.  Fall-through is almost never desired by the programmer, so in the rare case where it is, it is common practice to leave a comment stating that the fall-through is intentional.</p>
<p>In order to prevent fall-through, we have to use a break, a return, or a goto statement at the end of our case statements.  A return statement terminates the current function immediately, and a value is possibly returned to the caller.  This makes a lot of sense in short functions with a single purpose, such as the IsNumber() function example above.</p>
<p>However, it is often the case that we want to terminate the case statements without also terminating the entire function.  To do this, we use a break statement.  A <strong>break statement</strong> (declared using the <strong>break</strong> keyword) tells the compiler that we are done with this switch (or while, do while, or for loop), and execution continues with the statement after the end of the switch block.</p>
<p>Let&#8217;s look at our last example with break statements properly inserted:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<p></p>
<p><em>Warning: Forgetting the break statements in a switch block is one of the most common C++ mistakes made!</em></p>
<p><strong>Quiz</strong></p>
<p>1) Write a function called Calculate() that takes two integers and a char representing one of the following mathematical operations: +, -, /, or *.  Use a switch statement to perform the appropriate mathematical operation on the integers, and return the result.  If an invalid operator is passed into the function, the function should print &#8220;Error&#8221; and the program should exit (use the exit() function).</p>

</table>

		<p>Alex, could you show one or two programs from the examples above worked fully? for example, could you show how the code below might evaluate in the main function. Thanks. Also, shouldn&#8217;t the symbolic constant enumerators in the &#8220;enum Colors&#8221; block end with a &#8216;,&#8217; instead of a &#8216;;&#8217;?</p>
<pre>
enum Colors
{
    COLOR_BLACK;
    COLOR_WHITE;
    COLOR_RED;
    COLOR_GREEN;
    COLOR_BLUE;
};



void PrintColor(Colors eColor)
{
    using namespace std;
    switch (eColor)
    {
        case COLOR_BLACK:
            cout < < "Black";
            break;
        case COLOR_WHITE:
            cout << "White";
            break;
        case COLOR_RED:
            cout << "Red";
            break;
        case COLOR_GREEN:
            cout << "Green";
            break;
        case COLOR_BLUE:
            cout << "Blue";
            break;
        default:
            cout << "Unknown";
            break;
    }
}

int Main()
{

// Please show how the code in the above blocks might evaluate.

}

</PRE></pre>

		<div id="div-comment-7542" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-7542">
		February 8, 2008 at 10:03 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=7542#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-7542", "7542", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>As far as I can tell, all statements should be terminated by a semicolon, EXCEPT for compound statements (blocks).</p>
<p>A declaration is considered a statement, and thus should be terminated by a semicolon.  An enum is a declaration so it needs to be terminated with a semicolon.  Same with a class declaration.  The statements inside a switch are considered compound statements, so they do not need a terminating semicolon.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

<p></p>
<p>Will the other cases (e.g., addition of two integers) automatically convert the integer sum to a double return value without the compiler complaining?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-9608">
		<div id="div-comment-9608" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-9608">
		March 14, 2008 at 11:40 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=9608#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-9608", "9608", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Whether it&#8217;s more appropriate to return an int or a double depends entirely on your needs.  For some tasks, integer division might be exactly what you want.  Others, maybe not.  If your function is going to return a double, you might want to modify it to take double parameters as well so you can do floating point addition, subtraction, and multiplication.</p>
<p>I believe your case would work as you intend.  And yes, an integer return value will be implicitly converted to a double if the function has been declared to return a double.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-17916">
		<div id="div-comment-17916" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-17916">
		May 30, 2008 at 5:13 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=17916#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-17916", "17916", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I didn&#8217;t use break statements because I used return statements instead.  I wanted to return a different value to the caller for each case.  Keep in mind that return statements cause the function to immediately return to the caller, thus the switch statement will stop executing at that point.  Break is used to keep cases from overflowing into each other -- but this also happens with a return, since the entire function stops executing.  Thus, there&#8217;s no need to use a break statement in the cases where you are using a return.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

<p>class Car<br />

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-23168">

		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-23168">
		August 8, 2008 at 10:06 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=23168#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-23168", "23168", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Aah, you&#8217;ve run across a very interesting case here.  Case statements have to be statements that are essentially compile-time constants.  So something like this will work:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>This works because up is a constant at compile time.</p>
<p>However, in your case, your value of up is dependent upon the value of mUpKey, which can vary depending on the instance of Car.  So even though your value of up has been made const, it&#8217;s not a compile-time constant.</p>
		</div>

		<p>I am confussed with the following code. it is working fine. Can you explain the internal behavior of this code.. .How is works?<br />
 void duff(register char *to, register char *from, register int count)<br />
{<br />
        register int n=(count+7)/8;<br />
        switch(count%8)<br />
        {<br />
                case 0:<br />
                        do{<br />
                          *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 7:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 6:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 5:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 4:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 3:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 2:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                case 1:<br />
                        *to++ = *from++;<br />
                        }while( -n &gt;0);<br />
        }<br />
}</p>

}</p>

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-93100">
		<div id="div-comment-93100" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/68b2605ec65e9e0b6a5a5e0252575fa1?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/68b2605ec65e9e0b6a5a5e0252575fa1?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Jesper</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-93100">
		October 2, 2010 at 2:11 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=93100#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-93100", "93100", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Jesper'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hi Alex</p>
<p>I want to say that i love these tutorials you&#8217;ve made. I&#8217;ve been away from<br />
c++ for some years and I needed a brush-up and this is just perfect. Great job!!<br />
I have something to add to this section on the switch-case construct though.<br />
The real reason why there is two ways to achieve the same thing i.e. if-elseif-else and switch-case<br />
is because of execution-speed. if-elseif-else will always execute in linear time while switch-case<br />
is implemented using a jump-table meaning it will execute in constant time. Though the jump-table<br />
will only be used if the case-values are not spread out too far, because that would make the<br />
jump-table too big.<br />
So if it is possible you should always use switch-case and keep switch-values in the low range.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<div id="div-comment-97235" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/41bec191d2c11bbd24ecd4f402a992f6?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/41bec191d2c11bbd24ecd4f402a992f6?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Mythio</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-97235">
		April 9, 2012 at 5:24 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=97235#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-97235", "97235", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to Mythio'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Most obvious reason for not working would be that your not passing parameters to the calculate(); operation in the Input function.</p>
<p>Other stuff to look at for:</p>
<p>1. Input doesn&#8217;t return anything, i.e. it is not a function so use void Input();<br />
2. The call to calculate in main is not necessary (and missing parameters and wont work)<br />
3. The calculate function is called inside the input statement, however you need to use forward declaration of calculate() to make this work OR put calculate() before input().</p>
<p>Hope it helps, Mythio</p>
		</div>

		<p>#include<br />
#include </p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>float input1()<br />
{<br />
    cout&lt;&gt; x;<br />
    return x;<br />
}</p>
<p>float input2()<br />
{<br />
    cout&lt;&gt; x;<br />
    return x;<br />
}</p>
<p>char cOperator()<br />
{<br />
    cout&lt;&gt; Op;<br />
    return Op;<br />
}</p>
<p>float Result(float x, float y, char cOperator)<br />
{<br />
    switch (cOperator)<br />
    {<br />
        case &#8216;+&#8217; :<br />
        return x+y;<br />
        cout&lt;&lt; &quot;\nThe sum of &quot; &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; &quot; and &quot; &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; &quot; is: &quot; &lt;&lt; x+y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
        break;   <b>//reference 1</b><b></p>
<p>        case &#8216;-&#8216; :<br />
        return x-y;<br />
        cout&lt;&lt; &quot;\nThe subtraction of &quot; &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt;&quot; and &quot; &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; &quot; gives: &quot; &lt;&lt; x-y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
        break;</p>
<p>        case &#039;*&#039;:<br />
        return x*y;<br />
        cout&lt;&lt; &quot;\nThe product of &quot; &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; &quot; and &quot; &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; &quot; is: &quot; &lt;&lt; x*y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
        break;</p>
<p>        case &#039;/&#039;:<br />
        return x/y;<br />
        cout&lt;&lt; &quot;\nThe division of &quot; &lt;&lt; x &lt;&lt; &quot; and &quot; &lt;&lt; y &lt;&lt; &quot; gives: &quot; &lt;&lt; x/y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
        break;</p>
<p>        default:<br />
        cout&lt;&lt; &quot;Error!&quot; &lt;&lt;endl;<br />
        exit(1);<br />
    }</p>
<p>}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
    float number1 = input1();</p>
<p>    float number2 = input2();</p>
<p>    char Op = cOperator();</p>
<p>    Result(number1, number2, Op);</p>
<p>    cout&lt;&lt; Result(number1, number2, Op) &lt;&lt; endl;  </b><b>// reference 2</b><b></p>
<p>    return 0;</p>
<p>}</p>
<p>The above program compiles, but i wanted the &#8220;cout&#8221; (reference 1 ==&gt; look in the code) I defined under the cases in switch operator to be printed on the screen. Please anyone help, how do i do that?<br />
All I see is just the result printed as I defined in the main function (reference 2 ==&gt; check the comments in above code)</b></p>

		January 30, 2013 at 8:11 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=98145#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-98145", "98145", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to DrSuse'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Important!!<br />
Using the Gnu C++ compiler on Linux (can&#8217;t speak for other platforms), you must include a library in order for &#8220;exit(1)&#8221; to compile:</p>
<p>#include cstdlib (enclose &#8220;cstdlib&#8221; in the appropriate brackets)</p>
<p>Failure to do so will result in compiler errors:</p>
<p>error: &#8216;exit&#8217; was not defined in this scope.</p>
<p>Using stdlib.h (not stdlib) was also effective.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<p>int Calculate (int x, char a, int y){<br />
	switch (a){<br />
	case &#8216;+':<br />
		cout &lt;&lt; x + y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
		break;<br />
	case &#039;-&#039;:<br />
		cout &lt;&lt; x - y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
		break;<br />
	case &#039;/&#039;:<br />
		{<br />
			if (x == 0 || y == 0)<br />
				cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Cannot divide by zero.&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
			else<br />
				cout &lt;&lt; x / y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
		}<br />
		break;<br />
	case &#039;*&#039;:<br />
		cout &lt;&lt; x * y &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
		break;<br />
	default:<br />
		cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Did not enter valid operation.&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
		break;<br />
		return 0;<br />
	}<br />
}</p>
		</div>

		<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />
#include </p>
<p>using namespace std;</p>
<p>int getInt() // Gets an Integer and Returns it<br />
{<br />
	cout &lt;&gt; nInt;<br />
	return nInt;<br />
}</p>
<p>char getChar() //gets an Char and returns it<br />
{<br />
	cout &lt;&gt; cTransOp;<br />
	return cTransOp;<br />
}</p>
<p>double Calculate(int nX, int nY, char cOp)<br />
{<br />
	switch (cOp)<br />
	{<br />
	case &#8216;+':	return nX+nY;<br />
				break;<br />
	case &#8216;-&#8216;:	return nX-nY;<br />
				break;<br />
	case &#8216;*':	return nX*nY;<br />
				break;<br />
	case &#8216;/':	return nX/nY;<br />
				break;<br />
	default:	cout &lt;&lt; &quot;Error&quot; &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
				exit(-1);<br />
	}<br />
}</p>
<p>int main()<br />
{<br />
	int nX = getInt();<br />
	char cTransOp = getChar();<br />
	int nY = getInt();<br />
	double dResult = Calculate(nX, nY, cTransOp);<br />
	cout &lt;&lt; dResult;<br />
	return 0;<br />
}</p>
<p>Enter a number: 4<br />
Enter an Operator: -<br />
Enter a number: Error</p>
<p>Exit with Code -1 (0xffffffff)</p>

		<p>Hello all. I was curious as to why I can&#8217;t seem to get negative values to be calculated with the function. For example, if I put in 5 for my first number, a (-) sign, and any number &gt;5, (i.e. anything I expect to return a negative value) for the second, the program ends with exit code 253 but does not give a value (I also have the same issue with multiplication and division but feel subtraction is the simpler case). I tried explicitly initializing the integers as signed, but still can&#8217;t produce a negative number. Maybe I need to do something on the return line to specify a signed return value ? Any help would be appreciated.</p>

		<p>Your solution is missing breaks after each case&#8217;s return statement.</p>
<p><i>&#8220;Warning: Forgetting the break statements in a switch block is one of the most common C++ mistakes made!&#8221;</i></p>

		<li class="comment even thread-odd thread-alt depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-252213">
		<div id="div-comment-252213" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/d7037f2674eca8f29b16dbaea64691fd?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/d7037f2674eca8f29b16dbaea64691fd?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">kausthub</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/#comment-252213">
		April 22, 2015 at 1:18 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/53-switch-statements/?replytocom=252213#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252213", "252213", "respond", "74" )' aria-label='Reply to kausthub'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>#include &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;<br />
#include </p>
<p>using namespace std;<br />
int main(){<br />
switch (2)<br />
{<br />
   case 1: // Does not match -- skipped<br />
       cout &lt;&lt; 1 &lt;&lt; endl;<br />
	   break;<br />
   case 2: // Match!  Execution begins at the next statement<br />
       cout &lt;&lt; 2 &lt;&lt; endl; // Execution begins here<br />
	   break;<br />
   case 3:<br />
       cout &lt;&lt; 3 &lt;&lt; endl; // This is also executed<br />
	   break;<br />
   case 4:<br />
       cout &lt;&lt; 4 &lt;&lt; endl; // This is also executed<br />
	   break;<br />
   default:<br />
       cout &lt;&lt; 5 &lt;&lt; endl; // This is also executed<br />
	   break;<br />
}</p>
<p>Output:</p>
<p>fatal error C1075: end of file found before the left brace &#039;{&#039; at &#039;c:userskausthubdocumentsvisual studio 2010projectsquizquizquiz.cpp(7)&#039; was matched</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
